only increases — there is no method to decrease it.\"\"\"\n   579→        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=50)\n   580→        ledger.debit(10)\n   581→        ledger.debit(5)\n   582→ 586→        \"\"\"consumed never decreases across 15+ mixed operations.\"\"\"\n   587→        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=200)\n   588→        prev_consumed = 0\n   589→        ops = [\n   590→            (\"debit\", 10), (\"debit\", 5), (\"credit\", 3),\n   591→            (\"debit\", 20), (\"credit\", 10), (\"debit\", 1),\n   592→            (\"credit\", 0), (\"debit\", 15), (\"debit\", 0),\n   593→            (\"credit\", 5), (\"debit\", 8), (\"credit\", 2),\n   594→            (\"debit\", 12), (\"debit\", 3), (\"credit\", 7),\n   595→        ]\n   596→        for op, amount in ops:\n   597→            if op == \"debit\":\n   598→                ledger.debit(amount)\n   599→            else:\n   600→                ledger.credit(amount)\n   601→            assert ledger.consumed >= prev_consumed, (\n   602→                f\"consumed decreased from {prev_consumed} to {ledger.consumed} \"\n   603→                f\"after {op}({amount})\"\n   604→            )\n   605→            prev_consumed = ledger.consumed\n   606→\n   607→        # Verify final arithmetic\n   608→        total_debits = sum(a for o, a in ops if o == \"debit\")\n   609→        total_credits = sum(a for o, a in ops if o == \"credit\")\n   610→        assert ledger.consumed == total_debits\n   611→        assert ledger.reimbursed == total_credits\n   612→        assert ledger.available() == 200 - total_debits + total_credits\n   613→\n   614→    def test_exact_threshold_budget_can_launch(self):\n   615→        \"\"\"Budget exactly at minimum_allocation allows rate=0.8: net cost per passing task = 4 turns (spec §4.1).\"\"\"\n   626→        import math\n   627→\n   628→        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=200, reimbursement_rate=0.8)\n   629→        # Simulate one task: 8 turns consumed, then credit floor(8 * 0.8) = 6\n   630→        ledger.debit(8)\n   631→        reimbursed = math.floor(8 * ledger.reimbursement_rate)\n   632→        assert reimbursed == 6\n   633→        ledger.credit(reimbursed)\n   634→        # Also add 2 overhead turns\n   635→        ledger.debit(2)\n   636→        # Net cost = 8 + 2 - 6 = 4\n   637→        assert ledger.consumed == 10  # 8 + 2\n   638→        assert ledger.reimbursed == 6\n   639→        assert ledger.available() == 200 - 10 + 6  # = 196\n   640→\n   641→    def test_max_sustainable_tasks_at_08(self):\n   642→        \"\"\"Verify sustainability boundary: budget=200, rate=0.8, net_cost=4/task → ~50 tasks (spec §4.2).\"\"\"\n   643→        import math\n   644→\n   645→        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=200, reimbursement_rate=0.8, minimum_allocation=8)\n   646→        task_count = 0\n   647→        while ledger.can_launch():\n   648→            ledger.debit(8)\n   649→            reimbursed = math.floor(8 * ledger.reimbursement_rate)\n   650→            ledger.credit(reimbursed)\n   651→            ledger.debit(2)  # overhead\n   652→            task_count += 1\n   653→            if task_count > 100:  # safety bound\n   654→                break\n   655→        # 200 / 4 net cost = 50 total capacity, but can_launch requires minimum_allocation=8\n   656→        # After 49 tasks: available = 200 - 49*10 + 49*6 = 4 < 8, so loop exits at 49\n   657→        assert task_count == 49\n   658→        assert ledger.available() == 4\n   659→\n   660→    def test_46_task_sprint_sustainability(self):\n   661→        \"\"\"NFR-003: a 46-task sprint at rate=0.8, budget=200 completes with 16-turn margin.\"\"\"\n   662→        import math\n   663→\n   664→        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=200, reimbursement_rate=0.8)\n   665→        for _ in range(46):\n   666→            ledger.debit(8)\n   667→            reimbursed = test_budget_monotonicity_across_many_operations(self):\n        \"\"\"consumed never decreases across 15+ mixed operations.\"\"\"\n        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=200)\n        prev_consumed = 0\n        ops = [\n            (\"debit\", 10), (\"debit\", 5), (\"credit\", 3),\n            (\"debit\", 20), (\"credit\", 10), (\"debit\", 1),\n            (\"credit\", 0), (\"debit\", 15), (\"debit\", 0),\n            (\"credit\", 5), (\"debit\", 8), (\"credit\", 2),\n            (\"debit\", 12), (\"debit\", 3), (\"credit\", 7),\n        ]\n        for op, amount in ops:\n            if op == \"debit\":\n                ledger.debit(amount)\n            else:\n                ledger.credit(amount)\n            assert ledger.consumed >= prev_consumed, (\n                f\"consumed decreased from {prev_consumed} to {ledger.consumed} \"\n                f\"after {op}({amount})\"\n            )\n            prev_consumed = ledger.consumed\n\n        # Verify final arithmetic\n        total_debits = sum(a for o, a in ops if o == \"debit\")\n        total_credits = sum(a for o, a in ops if o == \"credit\")\n        assert ledger.consumed == total_debits\n        assert ledger.reimbursed == total_credits\n        assert ledger.available() == 200 - total_debits + total_credits\n\n    def test_exact_threshold_budget_can_launch(self):\n        \"\"\"Budget = 4 turns (spec §4.1).\"\"\"\n        import math\n\n        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=200, reimbursement_rate=0.8)\n        # Simulate one task: 8 turns consumed, then credit floor(8 * 0.8) = 6\n        ledger.debit(8)\n        reimbursed = math.floor(8 * ledger.reimbursement_rate)\n        assert reimbursed == 6\n        ledger.credit(reimbursed)\n        # Also add 2 overhead turns\n        ledger.debit(2)\n        # Net cost = 8 + 2 - 6 = 4\n        assert ledger.consumed == 10  # 8 + 2\n        assert ledger.reimbursed == 6\n        assert ledger.available() == 200 - 10 + 6  # = 196\n\n    def test_max_sustainable_tasks_at_08(self):\n        \"\"\"Verify sustainability boundary: budget=200, rate=0.8, net_cost=4/task → ~50 tasks (spec §4.2).\"\"\"\n        import math\n\n        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=200, reimbursement_rate=0.8, minimum_allocation=8)\n        task_count = 0\n        while ledger.can_launch():\n            ledger.debit(8)\n            reimbursed = math.floor(8 * ledger.reimbursement_rate)\n            ledger.credit(reimbursed)\n            ledger.debit(2)  # overhead\n            task_count += 1\n            if task_count > 100:  # safety bound\n                break\n        # 200 / 4 net cost = 50 total capacity, but can_launch requires minimum_allocation=8\n        # After 49 tasks: available = 200 - 49*10 + 49*6 = 4 < 8, so loop exits at 49\n        assert task_count == 49\n        assert ledger.available() == 4\n\n    def test_46_task_sprint_sustainability(self):\n        \"\"\"NFR-003: a 46-task sprint at rate=0.8, budget=200 completes with 16-turn margin.\"\"\"\n        import math\n\n        ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=200, reimbursement_rate=0.8)\n        for _ in range(46):\n            ledger.debit(8)\n            reimbursed = math.floor(8 * ledger.reimbursement_rate)\n            ledger.credit(reimbursed)\n            ledger.debit(2)  # overhead\n        assert ledger.available() > 0\n        # Expected: 200 - 46*(8+2) + 46*6 = 200 - 460 + 276 = 16\n        assert ledger.available() == 16\n\n    def test_budget_exhaustion_property(self):\n        \"\"\"NFR-008: for rate < 1.0, budget monotonically decays and reaches 0 in finite steps.\"\"\"\n        import math\n        import random\n\n        rng = random.Random(42)  # deterministic seed per R-005\n        for _ in range(20):  # 20 trials\n            budget = rng.randint(50, 500)\n            rate = round(rng.uniform(0.1, 0.99), 2)\n            turns_per_task = rng.randint(1, 50)\n            ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=budget, reimbursement_rate=rate, minimum_allocation=turns_per_task)\n\n            prev_available = ledger.available()\n            steps = 0\n            while ledger.can_launch() and steps < 10000:\n                ledger.debit(turns_per_task)\n                reimbursed = math.floor(turns_per_task * rate)\n                ledger.credit(reimbursed)\n                # Verify monotonic decay: each cycle net cost > 0\n                assert ledger.available() < prev_available, (\n                    f\"Budget did not decrease: {prev_available} -> {ledger.available()} \"\n                    f\"(rate={rate}, turns={turns_per_task})\"\n                )\n                prev_available = ledger.available()\n                steps += 1\n            # Budget must have been exhausted in finite steps\n            assert not ledger.can_launch(), f\"Budget never exhausted after {steps} steps\"\n\n    def test_rate_boundary_validation(self):\n        \"\"\"SC-001: verify TurnLedger behavior at rate boundary values.\"\"\"\n        import math\n\n        # rate=0.0 → zero reimbursement, valid\n        ledger_zero = TurnLedger(initial_budget=100, They are registered on the STRICT-tier\nGateCriteria instances.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nfrom ..pipeline.models import GateCriteria, SemanticCheck\n\n\n# --- Semantic check functions (pure: content -> bool) ---\n\ndef _no_heading_gaps(content: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Verify heading levels increment by at most 1 (no H2 -> H4 skip).\"\"\"\n    prev_level = 0\n    for line in content.splitlines():\n        stripped = line.lstrip()\n        if stripped.startswith(\"#\"):\n            level = 0\n            for ch in stripped:\n                if ch == \"#\":\n                    level += 1\n                else:\n                    break\n            if prev_level > 0 and level > prev_level + 1:\n                return False\n            prev_level = level\n    return True\n\n\ndef _cross_refs_resolve(content: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Verify all 'See section' / cross-reference patterns have matching headings.\n\n    Checks that internal references like 'See section X.Y' or 'See X.Y'\n    have corresponding headings. Unresolved references emit warnings but\n    do not block the pipeline (warning-only mode per OQ-001 for v2.20).\n    \"\"\"\n    import re\n    import warnings\n\n    # Extract heading anchors (simplified: heading text, lowercased)\n    headings: set[str] = set()\n    for line in content.splitlines():\n        stripped = line.lstrip()\n        if stripped.startswith(\"#\"):\n            heading_text = stripped.lstrip(\"#\").strip().lower()\n            headings.add(heading_text)\n\n    # Find cross-references like \"See section X\" or \"(see X.Y)\"\n    refs = re.findall(r'[Ss]ee\\s+(?:[Ss]ection\\s+)?[\"\\']?(\\d+(?:\\.\\d+)*)', content)\n    # If there are no cross-references, that's fine\n    if not refs:\n        return True\n\n    # Check each reference against headings\n    unresolved: list[str] = []\n    for ref in refs:\n        found = any(ref in h for h in headings)\n        if not found:\n            # Also check if the section number appears as a heading prefix\n            found = any(h.startswith(ref) for h in headings)\n        if not found:\n            unresolved.append(ref)\n\n    if unresolved:\n        for ref in unresolved:\n            warnings.warn(\n                f\"Unresolved cross-reference: 'See section {ref}' has no matching heading\",\n                stacklevel=2,\n            )\n        # Returns a formatted\n    45→    string suitable for terminal output per spec section 2.2 box layout.\n    46→\n    47→    Pure function: no I/O or side effects.\n    48→    \"\"\"\n    49→    blocking 52→\n    53→    lines: list[str] = []\n    54→    lines.append(\"=\" * 60)\n    55→    lines.append(\"  VALIDATION SUMMARY\")\n    56→    lines.append(\"=\" * 60)\n    57→    lines.append(\"\")\n lines.append(f\"  {f.id} | {f.description}\")\n    68→        lines.append(\"\")\n    69→\n    70→    if warning:\n    71→        lines.append(\"  --- WARNING ---\")\n    72→        for f in     for f in info:\n    79→            lines.append(f\"  {f.id} | {f.description}\")\n    80→        lines.append(\"\")\n    81→\n    82→    lines.append(\"=\" * 60)\n    83→    return \"\\n\".join(lines)\n    84→\n    85→\n    86→def should_skip_prompt(findings: list[Finding]) -> bool:\n    87→    \"\"\"Return True when prompt should be skipped (zero BLOCKING + zero WARNING).\n    88→\n    89→    Per spec section 2.2: when there are no BLOCKING and no WARNING findings,\n    90→    the prompt is auto-skipped.\n    91→\n    92→    Pure function: no I/O or side effects.\n    93→    \"\"\"\n    94→    blocking = sum(1 for f in findings if f.severity == \"BLOCKING\")\n    95→    warning = sum(1 for f in findings if f.severity == \"WARNING\")\n    96→    return blocking == 0 and warning == 0\n    97→\n    98→\n    99→def filter_findings(\n   100→    findings: list[Finding],\n   101→    scope: RemediationScope,\n   102→) -> tuple[list[Finding], list[Finding]]:\n   103→    \"\"\"Filter findings by user-selected scope with auto-SKIP logic.\n   104→\n   105→    Auto-SKIP is applied first: findings with agreement_category of\n   106→    NO_ACTION_REQUIRED or OUT_OF_SCOPE are always moved to skipped,\n   107→    regardless of scope selection.\n   108→\n   109→    Then scope filtering is applied:\n   110→    - BLOCKING_ONLY: keeps only BLOCKING severity\n   111→    - BLOCKING_WARNING: keeps BLOCKING + WARNING\n   112→    - ALL: keeps all findings that have fix_guidance\n   113→\n   114→    Returns (actionable, skipped) tuple.\n   115→\n   116→    Pure function: no I/O or side effects.\n   117→    \"\"\"\n   118→    actionable: list[Finding] = []\n   119→    skipped: list[Finding] = []\n   120→\n   121→    for f in findings:\n   122→        # Auto-SKIP: NO_ACTION_REQUIRED and OUT_OF_SCOPE always skipped\n   123→        if f.agreement_category in _AUTO_SKIP_CATEGORIES:\n   124→            skipped.append(f)\n   125→            continue\n   126→\n   127→        # Already terminal status (FIXED, SKIPPED) -> skip\n   128→        if f.status in (\"FIXED\", \"SKIPPED\"):\n   129→            skipped.append(f)\n   130→            continue\n   131→\n   132→        # Scope filtering\n   133→        if scope == RemediationScope.BLOCKING_ONLY:\n   134→            if f.severity == \"BLOCKING\":\n   135→                actionable.append(f)\n   136→            else:\n   137→                skipped.append(f)\n   138→        elif scope == RemediationScope.BLOCKING_WARNING:\n   139→            if f.severity in (\"BLOCKING\", \"WARNING\"):\n   140→                actionable.append(f)\n   141→            else:\n   142→                skipped.append(f)\n   143→        else:  # ALL\n   144→            if f.fix_guidance:\n   145→                actionable.append(f)\n   146→            else:\n   147→                skipped.append(f)\n   148→\n   149→    return actionable, skipped\n   150→\n   151→\n   152→def generate_remediation_tasklist(\n   153→    findings: list[Finding],\n   154→    source_report_path: str,\n   155→    source_report_content: str,\n   156→) -> str:\n   157→    \"\"\"Generate remediation-tasklist.md with YAML {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01W31mQyR8vLbvyvwNPJs7GF","type":"tool_result","content":"**FR-081**: A `_slip_count_matches_routing()` semantic check function SHALL be added to\n`gates.py`. The function:\n1. Parses frontmatter of `deviation-analysis.md` for `slip_count` (int)\n2. Parses `routing_fix_roadmap` field, splits on comma, strips whitespace, filters empty tokens\n3. If `slip_count == 0`: return `True` (empty routing is correct)\n4. If `slip_count > 0`: return `True` only if `len(routing_fix_roadmap_tokens) >= slip_count`\n5. Fails closed: missing or unparseable `slip_count` returns `False`\n\n**Rationale**: SLIPs that are counted but not routed are silently lost. This check is a\ncount-completeness gate: it verifies the routing list is at least as long as the SLIP count.\nIt does NOT verify that each SLIP ID is valid (that is FR-074's responsibility).\n\n**Failure message**:\n```\n\"slip_count is N but routing_fix_roadmap contains only M entries (M < N).\nAll SLIPs must appear in routing_fix_roadmap (FR-022).\nCheck deviation-analysis agent output for missing routing entries.\"\n```\n\nThis check SHALL be registered as a fifth semantic check on `DEVIATION_ANALYSIS_GATE` via\n`SemanticCheck(name=\"slip_count_matches_routing\", check_fn=_slip_count_matches_routing, ...)`,\nappended after the four checks added by FR-056/FR-057 (two original), FR-079 (third), FR-079\nfourth. The order is: `no_ambiguous_deviations`, `validation_complete_true`,\n`routing_consistent_with_slip_count`, `pre_approved_not_in_fix_roadmap`,\n`slip_count_matches_routing`.\n\n**Implementation note**: `len(tokens) >= slip_count` (not `==`) is intentional. It is possible\nfor the routing to contain IDs from both SLIP and INTENTIONAL-preference deviations. The count\nmay legitimately be higher than `slip_count` alone. A strict `==` check would produce false\npositives. Downstream, FR-075 cross-checks total routing length against `total_analyzed`.\n\n**FR-086**: A `_total_analyzed_consistent()` semantic check function SHALL be added to\n`gates.py`. The function validates that `total_analyzed == sum(pre_approved_count,\nintentional_count, slip_count, ambiguous_count)` in `deviation-analysis.md` frontmatter.\nImplementation follows the same pattern as `_total_annotated_consistent()` (FR-085) with\nthe corresponding field names.\n\nThis check SHALL be registered as a STRICT semantic check on `DEVIATION_ANALYSIS_GATE`\nvia `SemanticCheck(name=\"total_analyzed_consistent\", check_fn=_total_analyzed_consistent, ...)`,\nappended as the sixth semantic check (after `slip_count_matches_routing` from FR-081).\n\n**Failure message**: \"total_analyzed does not equal the sum of classification counts\n(pre_approved + intentional + slip + ambiguous). The deviation analysis artifact may be\nincomplete or incorrectly aggregated. Re-run deviation-analysis.\"\n\n**FR-088**: The `_routing_ids_valid()` function (FR-074) SHALL be extended to optionally\naccept a `spec_fidelity_content: str | None = None` second argument. When provided, the\nfunction SHALL additionally validate that every non-empty token in each routing field\nis present as a deviation ID in the `spec_fidelity_content` deviation table (parsed by\n`_extract_fidelity_deviations()` from FR-060).\n\nWhen `spec_fidelity_content` is `None` (backward-compatible default), the function performs\nonly format validation (the FR-074 behavior). When provided, it performs both format and\nexistence validation.\n\n**Gate integration**: `DEVIATION_ANALYSIS_GATE` SHALL pass `spec-fidelity.md` content as\n`aux_inputs` to `_routing_ids_valid()` when `GateCriteria.aux_inputs` is supported (see\nFR-079 Option A). If `aux_inputs` is not yet supported, this extension is deferred to the\nsame implementation milestone as FR-079 Option A.\n\n**Failure message (extended)**:\n```\n\"Routing ID(s) {ids} appear in routing_fix_roadmap but are not present in spec-fidelity.md.\nThese IDs cannot be remediated. Possible cause: deviation-analysis agent fabricated deviation IDs\nnot produced by spec-fidelity agent.
